## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic deformation laws and on temperature through thermal softening mechanisms. The combination suggests a constitutive model capturing both strain hardening and thermal effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varying linearly with T)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook strength (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturation hardening model)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (coupled power-law in strain and temperature)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Johnson-Cook full form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal term)
- Polynomial hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (quadratic hardening, linear thermal)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**c3 (nonlinear elastic-plastic transition)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (shifted power law with thermal term)
- Exponential softening model: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 + T)) (Arrhenius-like thermal dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (increasing stress with strain at decreasing rate) → Power-law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturation forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening (decreasing stress with temperature) → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (T_ref - T)**c or exp(-c*T)
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Additive decomposition: linear term (c*epsilon) plus nonlinear hardening term
- Separable strain-temperature coupling → Product form f(epsilon) * g(T), where strain and temperature effects are multiplicatively decomposed
- Yield point offset → Shifted strain variable (epsilon + c0)**c1 in Swift-type models to avoid zero-stress singularity
- Rate-independent plasticity at multiple temperatures → Family of stress-strain curves parameterized by T, suggesting T appears as a parameter in hardening coefficients
- Concave-up to concave-down stress-strain transition → Rational or sigmoidal forms in epsilon, such as epsilon/(c0 + epsilon)
- Linear thermal coefficient degradation → Elastic modulus or hardening parameters decrease linearly with T: (c0 - c1*T)
